$$

Each term of theso sums can bo integrated separately, giving

$$

$$

The parenthcses are the projections of tho areal velocities of the various bodies upon the lhrco fundamcntal planes (Arl. 16) As it is impossiblo to dotermine any fixcd point in spaco, so also it isimpossible to determine any fixed dircction in space,consequently it is impossihle to determine practically the constants C1,Cz, cg. Yet, in this case it is customary to assume that the fixed stars, on the average,do not ievolve in space,so that、by obsel ving them, these constants can bo determincd. It is evident, howovei, that there is no mole reason fol assuming that tho stars do not ievolve than there is for assuming that they aie not diifting through space,each being a pure assumplion without any possibihty of proof o1 dispioof.But it is to be noted that,if thcse assumptions are gianted, thc constants $c _ { 1 } , \ c _ { 2 } ,$ and $\pmb { c } _ { \mathbf { 3 } }$ can be delelmined canly with a high degrce of piecision,whilc in thc present slate of obsorvational Astionomy the constants of equations (4) oannot be found with any considerable accuracy.

Lct $A _ { 1 } , B _ { \nu } ,$ and ${ { \mathcal { C } } _ { \mathfrak { d } } }$ lepiesent the projections of tho aieas described by the lne fiom the oiigin lo the body m, upon thc cy,yz, and za-planes respectively; then (12) can be written

$$
\left\{ \begin{array} { l } { { \displaystyle \sum _ { i = 1 } ^ { n } m _ { \mathrm { i } } { \frac { d A _ { \mathrm { i } } } { d t } } = c _ { 1 } } , } \\ { { \displaystyle \sum _ { i = 1 } ^ { n } m _ { \mathrm { i } } { \frac { d B _ { \mathrm { i } } } { d t } } = c _ { 2 } } , } \\ { { \displaystyle \sum _ { i = 1 } ^ { n } m _ { \mathrm { i } } { \frac { d C _ { \mathrm { i } } } { d t } } = c _ { 3 } } , } \end{array} \right.
$$

the integrals of which are

$$
\left\{ \begin{array} { l l } { \displaystyle \sum _ { i = 1 } ^ { n } m _ { i } A _ { i } = c _ { 1 } t + c _ { 1 } \prime , } \\ { \displaystyle \sum _ { i = 1 } ^ { n } m _ { \ast } B _ { \ast } = c _ { 2 } t + c _ { 2 } \prime , } \\ { \displaystyle \sum _ { i = 1 } ^ { n } m _ { \ast } C _ { i } = c _ { 3 } t + c _ { 3 } \prime . } \end{array} \right.
$$
